| 2:15:50| So Councilman Roberto asked for visions, so here is a vision.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8150)|
| 2:15:58| Climate change unfolds as the largest game changer our city faces in terms of how we live and move.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8158)|
| 2:16:05| We witness an ever more massive reordering of our civilization| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8165)|
| 2:16:10| as we move deeper into the age of climate change.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8170)|
| 2:16:14| The policies and infrastructure that the city puts in place today| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8174)|
| 2:16:18| will have a large impact on how well Knoxville weathers the worsening storms.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8178)|
| 2:16:23| Future plans need to be focused both on reducing our carbon emissions| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8183)|
| 2:16:27| and to adapting to the all-encompassing effects of climate change.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8187)|
| 2:16:33| If we imagine the future will resemble the past,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8193)|
| 2:16:36| then we dangerously ignore the reality of climate change| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8196)|
| 2:16:40| and put ever more people in harm's way.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8200)|
| 2:16:43| It is critically important that we align our zoning map with transit-oriented development| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8203)|
| 2:16:49| so that the city has a bone structure we need to move toward a zero-carbon emissions economy by 2050.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8209)|
| 2:16:57| Zoning codes do affect our community's carbon emissions.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8217)|
| 2:17:01| Compact neighborhoods typically generate 20 to 40 percent less vehicle travel per capita| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8221)|
| 2:17:09| than conventional lower-density neighborhoods.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8229)|
| 2:17:12| An EPA study found that travel to a building often uses as much energy as consumed in the building.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8232)|
| 2:17:20| Residents reduce total building and transportation energy consumption 64 percent| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8240)|
| 2:17:27| by living in an attached energy-efficient green home in an urban location| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8247)|
| 2:17:33| and by 75 percent by living in a multifamily energy-efficient home| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8253)|
| 2:17:38| compared with the same household living in a typical detached single-family house| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8258)|
| 2:17:44| in an auto-dependent neighborhood.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8264)|
| 2:17:47| Housing location and type have greater impact on total energy use| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8267)|
| 2:17:52| than do vehicle or home energy efficiency.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8272)|
| 2:17:56| Transit-oriented development has many other benefits besides climate mitigation,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8276)|
| 2:18:02| affordable housing, strong transit systems, vibrant communities, and attraction of talent.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8282)|
| 2:18:08| Transforming the way our city develops is a long-term enterprise,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8288)|
| 2:18:12| but removing the zoning barriers to multifamily housing by right| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8292)|
| 2:18:17| and transit-oriented development opens the way for these infrastructural changes to occur| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8297)|
| 2:18:23| so that we may reap the benefits.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8303)|
| 2:18:26| Good news is that many within the city, especially our mobility agencies,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8306)|
| 2:18:31| understand and value transit-oriented development.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8311)|
| 2:18:34| Increasing density along our transit corridors, as pictured by CAT in its comments,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8314)|
| 2:18:40| is the important step that only RECODE Knoxville can take.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8320)|
| 2:18:44| Coupled with the city investments in these same areas to make them more equitable, walkable, and bikeable,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8324)|
| 2:18:51| we'll reduce carbon emissions and prepare our city for a climate-changing world.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/CityCouncilWorkshopR3877180920c?start=8331)|
